            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The utilization of renewable energies has become increasingly urgent for the sustainable development of our society.  Energy storage systems are essential in order to efficiently use these energies.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) show bright prospect in the application for energy storage markets due to the potential low cost originating from unlimited sources and wide distribution of Na.  However, the anode remains a great challenge in the industrialization of SIBs.  Hard carbon holds the most promising future among all reported anodes; however, there are still two main shortcomings such as high cost and low initial coulombic efficiency, which limit its application.  Here, we report a hard carbon material derived from an abundant and abandoned biomass of corn cobs (HCC) using a simple carbonization method.  The HCC shows excellent sodium storage performance with a reversible capacity of ca. 300 mA h g-1, a high initial coulombic efficiency of 86% and good cycling stability.  A prototype sodium-ion battery was prepd. to prove the application prospect using HCC1300 as the anode and Na0.9[Cu0.22Fe0.30Mn0.48]O2 as the cathode, exhibiting a high energy d. of 207 W h kg-1 and a long cycle life.  These excellent properties demonstrate that HCC is a potential candidate as an anode material for sodium-ion battery application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrzP3444VBrIbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgF8LOs6du_tA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1eju7nN&amp;md5=f6776d35bde5f3fb873f88fe495141b6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201600659"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Titirici, M.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hard Carbon Microtubes Made from Renewable Cotton as High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.         ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbons have become recently one of the most promising classes of anode materials for Na ion batteries (NIBs) owing to their high specific capacity and good cycling stability.  Among the precursors used to prep. hard C, phenolic resins are of great interest due to their high C yield, however, their toxicity must be overcome.  The authors propose a green, simple and scalable procedure to obtain phenolic resins which by pyrolysis at high temp. (&gt;1000°) result in eco-friendly hard carbons with low surface area, disordered structure and high C yield.  The influence of several synthesis parameters (type of solvent, thermopolymn./annealing temp. and gas flow) was studied to det. the impact on both phenolic resin and hard C characteristics.  The synthesis time (12 h-3 days) depends on the used solvent whereas the C yield (25-35%) on the crosslinking degree which could be controlled by adjusting both thermopolymn. temp. and atm.  The structure of the hard carbons mainly changed with the carbonization temp. (1100-1700°) while the texture of the material was sensitive to most of the studied parameters.  Stable reversible capacity up to 270 mA h g-1 and 100% coulombic efficiency (CE) after few cycles are obtained, demonstrating the potential for Na-ion applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq7kwe1Hfc2pLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgF8LOs6du_tA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXht1GmsLrK&amp;md5=11d925e13b5904589cee1f65b1e20779</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702434"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">3D Amorphous Carbon with Controlled Porous and Disordered Structures as a High-Rate Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Altering Thermal Transformation Pathway to Create Closed Pores in Coal-Derived Hard Carbon and Boosting of Na+ Plateau Storage for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Battery and Sodium-Ion Capacitor</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Kunfang; Sun, Fei; Wang, Hua; Wu, Dongyang; Chao, Yuxin; Gao, Jihui; Zhao, Guangbo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Coal features low-cost and high carbon yield and is considered as a promising precursor for carbon anode of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and sodium-ion capacitors (SICs).  Regulation of microcryst. state and pore configuration of coal structure during thermal transformation is key to boost Na+ storage behavior.  Herein, a facile strategy is reported to create abundant closed pores in anthracite-derived carbon that greatly improves Na+ plateau storage.  An altered thermal transformation pathway of chem. activation followed by high-temp. carbonization is adopted to achieve the conversion of open nanopores and ordered carbon crystallite into closed pores surrounded by short-range carbon structures.  The optimized sample delivers a large reversible capacity of 308 mAh g-1 that is dominantly contributed by the low-voltage plateau process.  Exptl. results reveal the enhanced pore-filling mechanism in the developed closed pores.  Benefitting from the improved plateau behavior, the constructed SIB delivers a high-energy d. of 231.2 Wh kg-1 with an av. voltage of 3.22 V; the assembled full-carbon SIC shows high energy and power densities (101.8 Wh kg-1 and 2.9 kW kg-1).  This work provides a universal thermal transformation approach for designing high-performance carbon anode with closed porosity from low-cost and highly arom. precursors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoiKE_89WOK5rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwtyr2-zaW0A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xit1aqs7vN&amp;md5=0f0e18e5380f927562d6bcc57a4b761d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201405370"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wickramaratne, N.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-dimensional N-doped graphene as anode material with superior cycle stability for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lin, Zhihua; Xiong, Xunhui; Zheng, Jie; Wang, Guanhua; Yang, Chenghao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">202</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A simple process has been proposed to prep. three-dimensional N-doped graphene.  The graphene shows outstanding performances when evaluated as anode for sodium ion battery, delivering a high reversible capacity of 405.2 mA h g-1 at 0.05 A g-1 and maintaining a retention of 100% up to 3700 cycles at 2 A g-1. D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nitrogen-rich hierarchically porous carbon as a high-rate anode material with ultra-stable cyclability and high capacity for capacitive sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>56</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">828</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">839</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2018.11.081</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D56%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D828-839%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DX.%2BHu%26author%3DX.%2BSun%26author%3DS.%2BJ.%2BYoo%26author%3DB.%2BEvanko%26author%3DF.%2BFan%26author%3DS.%2BCai%26author%3DC.%2BZheng%26author%3DW.%2BHu%26author%3DG.%2BD.%2BStucky%26title%3DNitrogen-rich%2Bhierarchically%2Bporous%2Bcarbon%2Bas%2Ba%2Bhigh-rate%2Banode%2Bmaterial%2Bwith%2Bultra-stable%2Bcyclability%2Band%2Bhigh%2Bcapacity%2Bfor%2Bcapacitive%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2018.11.081&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c02868&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2018.11.081&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-rich hierarchically porous carbon as a high-rate anode material with ultra-stable cyclability and high capacity for capacitive sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Xudong; Sun, Xiaohong; Yoo, Seung Joon; Evanko, Brian; Fan, Fengru; Cai, Shu; Zheng, Chunming; Hu, Wenbin; Stucky, Galen D.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">56</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">828-839</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon-based anode materials hold a promising future for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to their natural abundance and low cost of development.  In spite of carbon's important role in the commercialization of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), further exploration is necessary in order to find high-performance, high-rate carbon anode materials for SIBs.  A honeycomb-like, nitrogen-rich (17.72 at%), hierarchically porous, and highly disordered carbonaceous material (N-HC) with an expanded interlayer distance (0.44 nm in av.) is synthesized by spray drying and subsequent pyrolysis under flowing NH3.  The hierarchically porous structure and rich nitrogen doping result in a large sp. surface area (722 m2 g-1), more defects and active sites, and greater functional interface accessibility for the active porous carbonaceous material and electrolyte.  When N-HC is used as the anode material for SIBs, the batteries display favorable discharge capacities (255.9 mA h g-1 in the 3000th cycle at 500 mA g-1) and good capacitive-energy-storage behavior (67% at a scan rate of 0.5 mV s-1) with excellent high-rate performance and ultra-stable cyclability over 10,000 cycles at 5000 mA g-1.  Our results show that the combination of the hierarchically porous structure and nitrogen doping leads to improved energy storage by increasing the capacitive energy storage, which enhances the high-rate performance of N-HC.  To further enhance the performance of the material, an elec. pretreatment is employed to increase the initial Coulombic efficiency of N-HC to 79.5%, a record high for an SIB cell.  A full cell with an N-HC anode and a Na3V2(PO4)3/C cathode shows a high capacity with a favorable cyclability (238.7 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1 and a capacity retention of 95.3% compared to the second cycle).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo3JNYj3itp9rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwtyr2-zaW0A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXisFCisLnE&amp;md5=3d4836551425ccccb1ce250728574a60</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2012.12.072"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qie, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Functionalized N-doped interconnected carbon nanofibers as an anode material for sodium-ion storage with excellent performance</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>55</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">328</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">334</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pyrolysis of Cellulose under Ammonia Leads to Nitrogen-Doped Nanoporous Carbon Generated through Methane Formation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wei; Wang, Bao; Heron, Christopher G.; Allen, Marshall J.; Morre, Jeff; Maier, Claudia S.; Stickle, William F.; Ji, Xiulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Here, we present a simple one-step fabrication methodol. for nitrogen-doped (N-doped) nanoporous carbon membranes via annealing cellulose filter paper under NH3.  We found that nitrogen doping (up to 10.3 at %) occurs during cellulose pyrolysis under NH3 at as low as 550 °C.  At 700 °C or above, N-doped carbon further reacts with NH3, resulting in a large surface area (up to 1973.3 m2/g).                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Natural mushroom spores derived hard carbon plates for robust and low-potential sodium ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lyu, Taiyu; Lan, Xingxian; Liang, Lizhe; Lin, Xu; Hao, Chao; Pan, Zhiyi; Tian, Zhi Qun; Shen, Pei Kang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">365</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">137356</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Biomass derived hard C was considered a sustainable soln. for Na ion storage to improve the energy d. of Na ion batteries for low cost and large-scale energy storage.  However, developing this kind of C materials with high specific capacity at low-potential platform is a crit. issue.  Herein, a new structure of hard C plate was developed via pyrolysis of mushroom spore (Ganoderma lucidum).  The spore is mainly composed of chitin, distinguished from the lignin and cellulose in widely studied biomass.  The C plates obtained at 1400° have a suitable d002-spacing (0.371 nm) and ultra-low surface area down to 14.7 m2 g-1, resulting in a high reversible total discharge capacity of 305.8 mA h g-1 with an exceptional discharge capacity of 188.0 mA h g-1 at low-potential platform (0-0.1 V vs. Na+/Na) and excellent cycle stability as anode for SIBs.  Meanwhile, the proportion of low-potential capacity in total capacity is 61.5%, which is significantly superior to previously reported C materials prepd. using biomass from advanced plants.  Also, a full-cell constructed using the C plates as anode and Na vanadate phosphate as cathode further validates the outstanding Na+ storage performance at low-potential, in which the battery delivers a high working voltage of 3.25 V, approaching the discharge potential of 3.3 V of Na vanadate phosphate and a considerable energy d. of 199.2 W h kg-1 (based on the total mass of cathode and anode).  And also this high capacity for Na+ storage in the low potential range is attributed to the intercalation mechanism of NaC6 as the most possible intercalation compd.  The hard C derived from natural spores in the work presents a new route to design low cost and efficient C materials as advanced anode for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrKc0cbOJSmQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liOhkLG4Uw5rQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXit1Oiur%252FP&amp;md5=e999d79d64e7331767daa1883c0ec710</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1007/s12598-023-02607-3"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, M.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ang, E.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hard carbons for sodium-ion batteries: Structure, analysis, sustainability, and electrochemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dou, Xinwei; Hasa, Ivana; Saurel, Damien; Vaalma, Christoph; Wu, Liming; Buchholz, Daniel; Bresser, Dominic; Komaba, Shinichi; Passerini, Stefano</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today (Oxford, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">23</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">87-104</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MTOUAN</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Hard carbons are extensively studied for application as anode materials in sodium-ion batteries, but only recently a great interest has been focused toward the understanding of the sodium storage mechanism and the comprehension of the structure-function correlation.  Although several interesting mechanisms have been proposed, a general mechanism explaining the obsd. electrochem. processes is still missing, which is essentially originating from the remaining uncertainty on the complex hard carbons structure.  The achievement of an in-depth understanding of the processes occurring upon sodiation, however, is of great importance for a rational design of optimized anode materials.In this review, we aim at providing a comprehensive overview of the up-to-date known structural models of hard carbons and their correlation with the proposed models for the sodium-ion storage mechanisms.  In this regard, a particular focus is set on the most powerful anal. tools to study the structure of hard carbons (upon de-/sodiation) and a crit. discussion on how to interpret and perform such anal.  Targeting the eventual commercialization of hard carbon anodes for sodium-ion batteries - after having established a fundamental understanding - we close this review with a careful evaluation of potential strategies to ensure a high degree of sustainability, since this is undoubtedly a crucial parameter to take into account for the future large-scale prodn. of hard carbons.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoglanyMMwzlbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liOhkLG4Uw5rQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Identify the Removable Substructure in Carbon Activation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xing, Zhenyu; Qi, Yitong; Tian, Ziqi; Xu, Jing; Yuan, Yifei; Bommier, Clement; Lu, Jun; Tong, Wei; Jiang, De-en; Ji, Xiulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">29</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7288-7295</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Activated carbon plays a pivotal role in achieving crit. functions, such as sepn., catalysis, and energy storage.  A remaining question of carbon activation is which substructures in amorphous carbon are preferentially removed during activation.  Herein, we report the 1st structure-activation correlation elucidated on the basis of unprecedented comprehensive characterization on carbon activation.  We discover that activation under CO2 preferentially removes graphenic layers that are more defective.  Therefore, the resulting activated carbon contains thinned turbostratic nanodomains that are of a higher local graphenic order.  The mechanistic insights explain why more defective soft carbon is burned under CO2 at a much faster rate than hard carbon.  The mechanism leads to an activation-based design principle of mesoporous carbon.  Guided by this principle, a bimodal micromesoporous carbon is prepd. simply by CO2 activation.  Our findings may cause a paradigm shift for the rational design of nanoporous carbon.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpIWRO6cvO7n7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhL_z_VrxO18Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXht1GjtrrO&amp;md5=10cac5cff06b0336327165f8dac3abfe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201502217"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-rich porous carbon derived from biomass as a high performance anode material for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ou, Junke; Zhang, Yongzhi; Chen, Li; Zhao, Qian; Meng, Yan; Guo, Yong; Xiao, Dan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6534-6541</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen-rich porous carbon derived from ox horns has been successfully synthesized by an economically viable and an environmentally benign approach.  Such an ox horn derived carbon has a large surface area (BET surface area is 1300 m2/g), a unique three-dimensional porous nanostructure and a high inherent nitrogen content (5.5%).  The ox horn derived carbon, as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, exhibits superior electrochem. performances, such as a high reversible capacity (1181 mA-h/g at a c.d. of 100 mA/g) and a superior rate capability (304 mA-h/g at 5 A/g).  Furthermore, this study demonstrates the exploitation of a universal material in nature, i.e., ox horn, as a potential anode for the most sought after energy storage application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrbdmNSjVUDPbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhL_z_VrxO18Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXivVCksbw%253D&amp;md5=3e13d5c615a27898cadc773104f15931</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/eem2.12178"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chai, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Directional Oxygen Functionalization by Defect in Different Metamorphic-Grade Coal-Derived Carbon Materials for Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Directional Oxygen Functionalization by Defect in Different Metamorphic-Grade Coal-Derived Carbon Materials for Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Hanqing; Zhao, Dan; Ye, Jianqi; Wang, Pengfei; Chai, Maosheng; Li, Zhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">As the limiting factor for an energy storage technique from lab-scale to industrial-scale, cost means not only the price of raw materials but also the simplicity of processing technics.  In this work, the oxygen functionalized carbon materials were obtained from three representative different metamorphic-grade coals, i.e., lignite, bitumite, anthracite.  Oxygen functional groups like quinones, carboxylic anhydrides, and lactones are easier to form near defects according to the thermogravimetric-mass spectrometry measurements and d. functional theory calcn.  Considering the highest amt. of defects and C=O contained functional groups, the low metamorphic-grade lignite derived carbon exhibits a reversible capacity of 259.7 mA h g-1 after 50 cycles at 0.03 A g-1, best among these micron sized coal-based carbons.  The surface active sites contribute highly stable and majority of sodium storage capacity evidenced by in situ Raman spectra and cyclic voltammetry curves at different scan rates.  The coal-based carbon materials in this work offer options for industrial applications of sodium-ion battery anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq9J_onOMoh7rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhL_z_VrxO18Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhsFSlsbg%253D&amp;md5=01c5f390c085d459de4bfede82294b78</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1016/S0008-6223(98)00225-5"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lahaye, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nansé, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bagreev, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Strelko, V.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Porous structure and surface chemistry of nitrogen containing carbons from polymers</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1999</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>37</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">585</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">590</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Active carbons contg. up to 4.5% nitrogen (SCN-type carbons) were prepd. by carbonization in argon and steam activation of a vinylpyridine resin.  The porous structure of the SCN carbons with different burn-off values was characterized by gas adsorption (N2 and CO2), mercury porosimetry, and helium pycnometry.  The SCN carbons exhibit micro- and mesoporosities, which may be regulated.  Using microcalorimetric and water adsorption methods it was shown, that SCN carbons present a higher surface polarity than carbons without nitrogen.  The nitrogen atoms in the carbon structure behave as polar sites.  The nitrogen chem. investigated by XPS anal. is discussed.  The nitrogen chem. functions in SCN carbons are transformed during heat treatment.  In the char obtained at 1223 K and samples of activated carbons, the nitrogen is present in the six-membered rings of the polyarom. structures.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqrF4WLEqNreLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhL_z_VrxO18Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK1MXjtFSksL0%253D&amp;md5=7e669ea377d0879953dd491db4918a29</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2021.01.114"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kong, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">N/O double-doped biomass hard carbon material realizes fast and stable potassium ion storage</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>176</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">71</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">82</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">N/O double-doped biomass hard carbon material realizes fast and stable potassium ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Mengmeng; Kong, Qingquan; Feng, Wei; Yao, Weitang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, N/O co-doped cage-type biomass carbon (NOBC) was prepd. through a simple and facile hydrothermal reaction and two-step carbonization method.  As the anode of a potassium ion battery, NOBC displays a superhigh long-cycling performance and a super high rate performance.  NOBC-2 provides an excellent reversible capacity of 251.2 mAh g-1 after 1500 cycles at 0.5 A g-1, and an excellent performance of 334.6 mAh g-1 at a high c.d. of 5 A g-1 (after 2000 cycles).  The reversible capacity of 124.19 mAh g-1 can be maintained even after 5000 cycles at 10 A g-1.  The excellent performance of NOBC is attributed to the unique hollow cage structure, internal 3D carbon network structure and N/O co-doping.  Based on the results of detailed fundamental anal., the pseudo-capacitance mechanism contributes to the higher K ion storage process in NOBC-2.  D. functional theory (DFT) calcns. further show that N/O double doping can promote the adsorption of K ions in biomass carbon materials and improve the cond. of the materials.  The simple synthesis route and excellent electrochem. performance provide new insights for the search for novel carbon-based K storage anode materials with high energy and long cycle life.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoZO6mbE6CFB7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhL_z_VrxO18Q"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Probing the Energy Storage Mechanism of Quasi-Metallic Na in Hard Carbon for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Zhaohua; Feng, Xin; Bai, Ying; Yang, Haoyi; Dong, Ruiqi; Wang, Xinran; Xu, Huajie; Wang, Qiyu; Li, Hong; Gao, Hongcai; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon (HC) is the most promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), nevertheless, the understanding of sodium storage mechanism in HC is very limited.  As an important aspect of storage mechanism, the steady state of sodium stored in HC has not been revealed clearly to date.  Herein, the formation mechanism of quasi-metallic sodium and the quasi-ionic bond between sodium and carbon within the electrochem. reaction on the basis of theor. calcns. are disclosed.  The presence of quasi-metallic sodium is further confirmed with the assistance of a specific reaction between the sodiated HC electrode and ethanol, by analyzing the reaction products with Fourier-transform IR spectroscopy, gas chromatog., and NMR.  Moreover, based on the specific chem. reaction, the compn. of fully sodiated HC is estd. to be NaC6.7, and the corresponding capacity of sucrose-derived HC is calcd. to be 333.4 mAh g-1 in SIBs, matching well with the exptl. result.  This work helps to reveal the steady state of sodium and improve the understanding of sodium storage behavior in HC from the aspect of charge transfer. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2200886</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.202200886</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D12%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D2200886%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26author%3DX.%2BChen%26author%3DJ.%2BTian%26author%3DP.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BFang%26author%3DY.%2BFang%26author%3DX.%2BLiang%26author%3DJ.%2BFeng%26author%3DJ.%2BDong%26author%3DX.%2BAi%26author%3DH.%2BYang%26author%3DY.%2BCao%26title%3DAn%2BOverall%2BUnderstanding%2Bof%2BSodium%2BStorage%2BBehaviors%2Bin%2BHard%2BCarbons%2Bby%2Ban%2B%25E2%2580%25B3Adsorption-Intercalation%252FFilling%25E2%2580%25B3%2BHybrid%2BMechanism%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.202200886&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c02868&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.202200886&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Overall understanding of sodium storage behaviors in hard carbon by adsorption-intercalation/filling hybrid mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Xiaoyang; Tian, Jiyu; Li, Peng; Fang, Youlong; Fang, Yongjin; Liang, Xinmiao; Feng, Jiwen; Dong, Jiao; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">24</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2200886</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon has the potential to serve as a high-capacity anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), however, its Na+ storage mechanism, particularly on the low potential plateau, remains controversial.  To overcome this issue, two types of hard carbons with different microstructures are employed and the relationship between the microstructures and Na+ storage behaviors is evaluated.  By the combination of operando X-ray diffraction, ex situ Raman spectroscopy, NMR, and theor. calcn., it is found that the sodium storage capacities of the hard carbons in the low potential plateau region contain the concurrent contributions from both interlayer intercalation and micropores filling, and the ratio of the two contributors greatly depends on the microstructure of hard carbon materials.  Moreover, an electrochem. pointer (potential inflection point at the end of the discharge curve) is found to distinguish the dominance of interlayer intercalation and the micropores filling processes of sodium ions in the low potential plateau region.  Based on this new finding, a microstructure-dependent mechanism ("adsorption-intercalation/filling" hybrid mechanism) is proposed to achieve an overall understanding of the sodium storage behaviors in different hard carbon materials, which may provide deep insight into the rational design of hard carbon structures as high-performance anode materials for advanced SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrd5o_TaI-O_7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljt6jp5KELE5Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xht1agu7nK&amp;md5=9f95b49d8ff9183780d72d7341aea49b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Murata, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ishikawa, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yabuuchi, N.</span></span>;                 10.1002/adfm.201100854</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D21%26publication_year%3D2011%26pages%3D3859-3867%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26author%3DS.%2BKomaba%26author%3DW.%2BMurata%26author%3DT.%2BIshikawa%26author%3DN.%2BYabuuchi%26author%3DT.%2BOzeki%26author%3DT.%2BNakayama%26author%3DA.%2BOgata%26author%3DK.%2BGotoh%26author%3DK.%2BFujiwara%26title%3DElectrochemical%2BNa%2BInsertion%2Band%2BSolid%2BElectrolyte%2BInterphase%2Bfor%2BHard-Carbon%2BElectrodes%2Band%2BApplication%2Bto%2BNa-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.201100854&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c02868&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.201100854&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical Na Insertion and Solid Electrolyte Interphase for Hard-Carbon Electrodes and Application to Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Komaba, Shinichi; Murata, Wataru; Ishikawa, Toru; Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Ozeki, Tomoaki; Nakayama, Tetsuri; Ogata, Atsushi; Gotoh, Kazuma; Fujiwara, Kazuya</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">21</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3859-3867</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, lithium-ion batteries were attracting more interest for use in automotive applications.  Lithium resources are confirmed to be unevenly distributed in South America, and the cost of the lithium raw materials has roughly doubled from the first practical application in 1991 to the present and is increasing due to global demand for lithium-ion accumulators.  Since the electrochem. equiv. and std. potential of sodium are the most advantageous after lithium, sodium based energy storage is of great interest to realize lithium-free high energy and high voltage batteries.  However, to the best of authors knowledge, there were no successful reports on electrochem. sodium insertion materials for battery applications; the major challenge is the neg. electrode and its passivation.  In this study, high capacity and excellent reversibility are achieved of sodium-insertion performance of hard-carbon and layered NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 electrodes in propylene carbonate electrolyte solns.  The structural change and passivation for hard-carbon are investigated to study the reversible sodium insertion.  The 3-V secondary Na-ion battery possessing environmental and cost friendliness, Na+-shuttlecock hard-carbon/NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 cell, demonstrates steady cycling performance as next generation secondary batteries and an alternative to Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrp5J70QNujrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljt6jp5KELE5Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhtVWjurfM&amp;md5=be5cae72214fa773ada0e3fcca7b49d1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201300680"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Soll, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fellinger, T.-P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Antonietti, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Water Dispersible, Highly Graphitic and Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanobubbles</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4135</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4141</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Water Dispersible, Highly Graphitic and Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanobubbles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Soll, Sebastian; Fellinger, Tim-Patrick; Wang, Xinchen; Zhao, Qiang; Antonietti, Markus; Yuan, Jiayin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile synthetic route to highly dispersible, nitrogen-doped carbon nanobubbles with sizes from 90 down to 25 nm was demonstrated.  Gram scale prodn. has already been realized on a lab. base, which is out of the range of most other prepn. methods for similar nanostructures.  These nanospheres adopt an unusual shape-fitting graphitic structure in which a unique radial packing order of graphene layers offers direct and amplified access to the edge structures at the particle surface.  All these make them unparalleled by any other known carbon nanostructures in terms of colloidal stability, electronic cond., and potentially electronic interaction.  They could serve efficiently as metal-free catalysts for oxygen redn. in electrocatalysis.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp7URLGoHI1PrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljt6jp5KELE5Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFShtLnJ&amp;md5=64c9ee3c1969e377fa91c8071a266538</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-022-4708-5"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.-P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, H.-R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, Y.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, F.-F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Self-supported hard carbon anode from fungus-treated basswood towards sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Nano Res.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3832</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3838</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hard Carbon Fibers Pyrolyzed from Wool as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Xiaoming; Li, Qian; Qiu, Shen; Liu, Xiaoling; Xiao, Lifen; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">JOM</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this paper, we first demonstrate that the wool from worn-out clothes can serve as a low-cost and easy-to-collect precursor to prepg. high-performance hard carbons for Na-ion batteries.  Morphol. characterizations demonstrate that this wool-derived hard carbon presents well-defined and homogeneously dispersed fiber networks.  X-ray diffraction results combined with high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy anal. reveal that the interlayer space (d(002)) of the graphitic layers is 0.376 nm, sufficient for Na insertion into the stacked graphene layers.  Electrochem. results show that the wool-derived hard carbon can deliver a high capacity of 303 mAh g-1 and excellent cycle stability over 80 cycles.  This satisfactory electrochem. performance and easy synthetic procedure make it a promising anode material for practical SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqcrgDiMXh11LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMDgCOuNTORA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xhtlals7%252FE&amp;md5=69a84bfad54192c6d7c172a9f7a08027</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1016/j.susmat.2022.e00446"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hard carbon derived from hazelnut shell with facile HCl treatment as high-initial-coulombic-efficiency anode for sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>Sustainable Mater.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hard carbon derived from hazelnut shell with facile HCl treatment as high-initial-coulombic-efficiency anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jiacheng; Zhao, Jiahua; He, Xiangxi; Qiao, Yun; Li, Li; Chou, Shu-Lei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Sustainable Materials and Technologies</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">33</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon is an extremely promising anode material for Na-ion batteries owing to its low cost and low operating potential plateau.  However, the practical use of hard carbon materials in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is greatly constrained by their low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE).  Biomass as carbon sources are a good choice due to the abundance of resources and natural microstructure.  Regrettably, biomass contains many impurities that lower its electrochem. performance.  Here, by facile synthesis methods, we prep. a hard carbon with a high reversible capacity of 342 mA h g-1 and a high ICE of 91%.  The hard carbon is obtained by carbonizing a low-cost biomass hazelnut shell under hydrochloric acid treatment.  Hydrochloric acid treatment removes impurities and change microstructure such as interlayer spacing and active sites.  The results reveal that the active site and interlayer spacing of the hard carbon material was raised with hydrochloric acid treatment.  Therefore, the reversible capacity of hard carbon was greatly improved by the hydrochloric acid treatment.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrB1CyaTzGexrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMDgCOuNTORA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xit1SmtrjM&amp;md5=0645dbdfb269d606831757d1dbeca226</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA01394A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahbi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kiso, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Horiba, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chafik, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hida, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Matsuyama, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synthesis of hard carbon from argan shells for Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of hard carbon from argan shells for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dahbi, Mouad; Kiso, Manami; Kubota, Kei; Horiba, Tatsuo; Chafik, Tarik; Hida, Kazuo; Matsuyama, Takashi; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon is an attractive material for neg. electrodes in sodium-ion batteries.  Herein, we report a new hard carbon synthesized via carbonization of argan shell biomass, which delivers an enhanced capacity higher than 330 mA h g-1 based upon reversible sodium insertion.  We prepd. hard carbon under different high-temp. treatment and biomass pretreatment conditions.  The graphitization degree of the hard carbon increased as the carbonization temp. increased; simultaneously, the reversible capacity for sodium storage was significantly influenced by the carbonization temp.  Structural characterization revealed differences in the structures of the hard carbons synthesized at different carbonization temps., which elucidates the correlation between the increased capacity and the micropore size available for sodium storage.  The composite electrodes contg. the argan hard carbons with a sodium polyacrylate binder were tested in non-aq. sodium half cells.  The electrodes delivered reversible capacities as high as 300 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 25 mA g-1 with superior reversibility and capacity retention of 94.1% after 70 cycles.  By carbonization of argan shell biomass treated with HCl aq. soln., we successfully demonstrated a higher reversible capacity of 333 mA h g-1 and an excellent capacity retention of 96.0% after 100 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqX1TPMHOOIIbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMDgCOuNTORA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXmt1Khtro%253D&amp;md5=b0ca64543d4af15de4d6f10cfea4ba7b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b11627"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Insights into the Surface Oxygen Functional Group-Driven Fast and Stable Sodium Adsorption on Carbon</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater.                 10.1021/acsami.9b11627</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D12%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D6991-7000%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DH.%2BZhao%26author%3DJ.%2BYe%26author%3DW.%2BSong%26author%3DD.%2BZhao%26author%3DM.%2BKang%26author%3DH.%2BShen%26author%3DZ.%2BLi%26title%3DInsights%2Binto%2Bthe%2BSurface%2BOxygen%2BFunctional%2BGroup-Driven%2BFast%2Band%2BStable%2BSodium%2BAdsorption%2Bon%2BCarbon%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.9b11627&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c02868&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.9b11627&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Insights into the Surface Oxygen Functional Group-Driven Fast and Stable Sodium Adsorption on Carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Hanqing; Ye, Jianqi; Song, Wei; Zhao, Dan; Kang, Mengmeng; Shen, Hanting; Li, Zhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6991-7000</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Engineering the oxygen functional groups (OFGs) is a dynamic strategy to tune the surface chem. and electrochem. properties of carbon-based materials.  In this paper, the species and contents of OFGs on the surface of ordered mesoporous carbon (OMC) and their effects on the sodium storage performance are systematically investigated without the interference of interlayer distance variation, extrinsic defects, other heteroatoms (e.g., N, S), etc.  Theor. calcns. performed on various OFGs demonstrate that quinones and carboxylic anhydride groups possess two C=O bonds with stable configurations, good electronic cond., and strong sodium adsorption capability, contributing greatly to the Na+ storage capacity compared to the carboxylic acid groups.  The ex situ techniques disclose the evolution of the OFGs and manifest the stable coordination of Na+ with C=O bonds even after long cycles.  The optimized OFGs boost the Na+ redox reaction kinetics and enhance the surface capacitance contribution, achieving a capacity enhancement of 64.7% compared to the pristine OMC.  This work would present implications in rational designing of oxygen-functionalized carbon materials for energy storage fields.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrDwoPiy6XBZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMDgCOuNTORA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtlWnsL0%253D&amp;md5=2986ab98940ea2aad3541a658205d959</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1039/c2ee23599d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Holt, C.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mesoporous nitrogen-rich carbons derived from protein for ultra-high capacity battery anodes and supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zhi; Xu, Zhanwei; Tan, Xuehai; Wang, Huanlei; Holt, Chris M. B.; Stephenson, Tyler; Olsen, Brian C.; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work we demonstrate that biomass-derived proteins serve as an ideal precursor for synthesizing carbon materials for energy applications.  The unique compn. and structure of the carbons resulted in very promising electrochem. energy storage performance.  We obtained a reversible lithium storage capacity of 1780 mA h g-1, which is among the highest ever reported for any carbon-based electrode.  Tested as a supercapacitor, the carbons exhibited a capacitance of 390 F g-1, with an excellent cycle life (7% loss after 10 000 cycles).  Such exquisite properties may be attributed to a unique combination of a high sp. surface area, partial graphitization and very high bulk nitrogen content.  It is a major challenge to derive carbons possessing all three attributes.  By templating the structure of mesoporous cellular foam with egg white-derived proteins, we were able to obtain hierarchically mesoporous (pores centered at ∼4 nm and at 20-30 nm) partially graphitized carbons with a surface area of 805.7 m2 g-1 and a bulk N-content of 10.1 wt%.  When the best performing sample was heated in Ar to eliminate most of the nitrogen, the Li storage capacity and the specific capacitance dropped to 716 mA h g-1 and 80 F g-1, resp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpWc3QQt5xj97Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhv_SkYDS1Y4g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXivVGktrY%253D&amp;md5=79ec295fd627390520246896f7b45a7a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1021/nl3016957"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sushko, M.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Ion Insertion in Hollow Carbon Nanowires for Battery Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Yuliang; Xiao, Lifen; Sushko, Maria L.; Wang, Wei; Schwenzer, Birgit; Xiao, Jie; Nie, Zimin; Saraf, Laxmikant V.; Yang, Zhengguo; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hollow carbon nanowires were prepd. by pyrolysis of a hollow polyaniline nanowire precursor.  The hollow carbon nanowires used as anode material for Na-ion batteries deliver a high reversible capacity of 251 mA-h/g and 82.2% capacity retention over 400 charge-discharge cycles between 1.2 and 0.01 V (vs. Na+/Na) at a const. current of 50 mA/g (0.2C).                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Expanded graphite as superior anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wen, Yang; He, Kai; Zhu, Yujie; Han, Fudong; Xu, Yunhua; Matsuda, Isamu; Ishii, Yoshitaka; Cumings, John; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite, as the most common anode for com. Li-ion batteries, has been reported to have a very low capacity when used as a Na-ion battery anode.  It is well known that electrochem. insertion of Na+ into graphite is significantly hindered by the insufficient interlayer spacing.  Here we report expanded graphite as a Na-ion battery anode.  Prepd. through a process of oxidn. and partial redn. on graphite, expanded graphite has an enlarged interlayer lattice distance of 4.3 Å yet retains an analogous long-range-ordered layered structure to graphite.  In situ transmission electron microscopy has demonstrated that the Na-ion can be reversibly inserted into and extd. from expanded graphite.  Galvanostatic studies show that expanded graphite can deliver a high reversible capacity of 284 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 20 mA g-1, maintain a capacity of 184 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, and retain 73.92% of its capacity after 2,000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFEZ8wJYk1irVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhv_SkYDS1Y4g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXksVeqs7g%253D&amp;md5=e4bc2edac8d22121e7986e165b7df007</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201901261"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vasileff, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiao, S.-Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Graphitic Carbon Nitride (g-C3N4)-Derived N-Rich Graphene with Tuneable Interlayer Distance as a High-Rate Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Storage Mechanism of Nongraphitic Carbons: A General Model and the Function of Accessible Closed Pores</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yuan, Man; Cao, Bin; Liu, Huan; Meng, Chenyang; Wu, Jianping; Zhang, Su; Li, Ang; Chen, Xiaohong; Song, Huaihe</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nowadays, the sodium storage mechanism of nongraphitic carbon materials still remains controversial despite their promising application as anode materials in sodium-ion batteries.  Herein, a series of hard carbons and soft carbons with different crystallinities and pore structures was prepd. from coal tar pitch, and a general mechanism is proposed through the anal. and contrast of their microstructures and electrochem. performances.  In particular, it was found that sodium adsorption and insertion take place in the form of sloping capacity for both soft carbons and hard carbons, while sodium closed pore filling only exists below 0.1 V in hard carbons corresponding to the plateau capacity.  Moreover, we further propose the concept of accessible closed pores (ACPs) and quantify the surface area of ACPs, which exhibits a high linear correlation with the plateau capacity.                             cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201903176"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Morikawa, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nishimura, S.-i.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hashimoto, R.-i.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ohnuma, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yamada, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Mechanism of Sodium Storage in Hard Carbon: An X-Ray Scattering Analysis</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1903176</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.201903176</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D1903176%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26author%3DY.%2BMorikawa%26author%3DS.-i.%2BNishimura%26author%3DR.-i.%2BHashimoto%26author%3DM.%2BOhnuma%26author%3DA.%2BYamada%26title%3DMechanism%2Bof%2BSodium%2BStorage%2Bin%2BHard%2BCarbon%253A%2BAn%2BX-Ray%2BScattering%2BAnalysis%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.201903176&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c02868&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.201903176&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mechanism of Sodium Storage in Hard Carbon: An X-Ray Scattering Analysis</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Morikawa, Yusuke; Nishimura, Shin-ichi; Hashimoto, Ryu-ichi; Ohnuma, Masato; Yamada, Atsuo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1903176</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon is a std. anode material for Na-ion batteries.  However, its low crystallinity and diverse microstructures make obtaining a full understanding of the sodium storage mechanism challenging.  Here, the results of a systematic ex situ small and wide angle X-ray scattering study of a series of nanostructured hard carbons, which reveal clear evidence of sodium storage in the graphene-graphene interlayers and nanopores, are presented.  Particularly, an emergence of a broad peak around q ≈ 2.0-2.1 Å-1 in the low voltage region is suggested to be an indicator that sodium is densely confined in the nanopores.  Thus, classical X-ray scattering techniques are demonstrated to be effective in elucidating the overall reaction scheme of Na insertion into hard carbon.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp-FRJaunl-87Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhv_SkYDS1Y4g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitlegt7zL&amp;md5=d5a39933f2694238d874afdd1411bd61</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script
